<div id="review_172438853" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172438853" />
    <a title="christa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40816-christa"><img alt="christa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349499447p2/40816.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172438853?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="christa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="christa" href="/user/show/40816-christa">christa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172438853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3085528023583344663">I just stopped hating Daniel Clowes' graphic novel "Ghost World" like 7 minutes ago. Literally. I've had a long history of hating the listless bitches Enid and Rebecca and their ironic diner hopping, misfit hounding and personality contriving. But it just went away. Like a decade-old hate fever that finally broke.<br/><br/>Fact: My boyfriend and I rarely fight. So rarely that I can remember that we did have a fight in 2007 while watching the movie "Ghost World" about how much I hated the movie "Ghost Worl</span>
  <span id="freeText3085528023583344663" style="display:none">I just stopped hating Daniel Clowes' graphic novel "Ghost World" like 7 minutes ago. Literally. I've had a long history of hating the listless bitches Enid and Rebecca and their ironic diner hopping, misfit hounding and personality contriving. But it just went away. Like a decade-old hate fever that finally broke.<br /><br />Fact: My boyfriend and I rarely fight. So rarely that I can remember that we did have a fight in 2007 while watching the movie "Ghost World" about how much I hated the movie "Ghost World." It was a lot of me ranting, not unlike Enid, and him confused at my outburst.<br />Other fact: I was drunk.<br /><br />When a person decides to pull up a chair up to the whole graphic novels table, and when a person divulges that this new interest probably won't include books with Super Werewolves and Masked Crusaders, people already at the table will recommend "Ghost World." If a person adds a few graphic novels to her Amazon Wish List, Amazon will recommend "Ghost World." It is, apparently, part of the canon. Strangers will recommend "Ghost World." It might be the most readily available of graphic novels.<br /><br />I got about a quarter of the way into "Ghost World" about two weeks ago, sighing and eye rolling all while getting really stoked about finally reading something I hate. I could really get in there and hate it super hard all over the internet. It's been far too long. I've been cursed by a steady stream of three-star or better picks. Blerg. Boring. I set "Ghost World" aside for whatever reason and when I picked it up again I started at the beginning. And ... nothing. No throbbing forehead veins. My blood didn't simmer. No eye rolling. I thought about Enid, her ever-changing hair and style statements, following people she believes are satanists around the grocery store to see what satanists eat and having a snarky comment and mean-spirited nickname about every person who falls into her field of vision.<br /><br />Nothing. In fact, I laughed.<br /><br />The story is mini chapters in the life of best friends Enid and Rebecca. They're droll and bored and boring and they sprawl on beds and talk and bitch about models in magazines and they go to diners and make up stories about the other regulars. Sometimes they wander around and do stuff. But mostly they're in this limbo between high school and college and so close they wonder if its healthy. They abuse the pushover guy friend. They dream of walking into a sex shop and looking around. At one point Enid really gets into the cartoonist Daniel Clowes.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong. They are still unlikable little snots I'm glad I didn't sit next to in homeroom. But there are some truly great scenes. Enid tries to muster some romantic nighttime feelings for a teacher, testing and ditching out on different scenarios in her head when she's in bed -- including one that finds him fully clothed in the shower with her -- before finally falling asleep without consummating the sexy visual. Or, during a conversation about a guy Enid and Rebecca know who is totally into politics, Enid apes a conversation with him:<br /><br />"Yeah Jason, ever since you stopped eating meat and bathing and started doing grafitti and fucking up ATM machines, the world has become a way better place."<br /><br />So I stand corrected. "Ghost World" isn't terrible. It certainly isn't anything to fight about. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3085528023583344663" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_131944111" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131944111" />
    <a title="J. Gonzalez- Blitz " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4571613-j-gonzalez--blitz"><img alt="J. Gonzalez- Blitz " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593718044p2/4571613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131944111?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J. Gonzalez- Blitz " class="user" itemprop="url" name="J. Gonzalez- Blitz " href="/user/show/4571613-j-gonzalez--blitz">J. Gonzalez- Blitz </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4571613-j-gonzalez--blitz?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4571613-j-gonzalez--blitz?shelf=teen">teen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131944111" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17555870964207149894">A male friend of mine once commented that the main characters of Ghost World didn't seem authentic because "their interests didn't seem to ring true for teenage girls". Actually,it's more that their interests didn't follow the spoon fed formula that most media TELLS us are the interests of most teenage girls. This is not a book about dating, makeovers, and popularity. It is the story of two sort of quirky girls who are above average intelligence(though not quite brilliant or anything)in a town t</span>
  <span id="freeText17555870964207149894" style="display:none">A male friend of mine once commented that the main characters of Ghost World didn't seem authentic because "their interests didn't seem to ring true for teenage girls". Actually,it's more that their interests didn't follow the spoon fed formula that most media TELLS us are the interests of most teenage girls. This is not a book about dating, makeovers, and popularity. It is the story of two sort of quirky girls who are above average intelligence(though not quite brilliant or anything)in a town that holds nothing for them. So to pass the time they snidely mock former classmates who pretty much deserve their disdain-the semi-political would be actress who betrays her ideals in a heartbeat if it gets her a spot in a commercial. Or the constantly striving-to-be-shocking zinester who seems to fancy himself the next Jim Goad with his obsessions of racism and pedophiles. Or else they spend time imagining people to be "Satanists" or what have you in order to spice up a fairly bland existence. Trouble is, Enid and Rebecca aren't exactly the lovable-outcast-against-the-system types often found in teen dramas of this sort either. They often seem as empty in their own ways as the people they goof on. Neither of them seems to have any ambitions or desires of their own as they wander about their town post high school. Enid expresses a vague desire to go to a new place and become a whole new person, but what sort of person exactly? Ultimately Enid and Rebecca aren't passionate about anything outside of their own waning friendship--every activity they consume is not because they genuinely enjoy it, but because it's oh-so "ironic" - the horrible comedian, the badly done 50's diner. Is this really living? Maybe that's why this is a "Ghost World".</span>
  <a data-text-id="17555870964207149894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_216252129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/216252129" />
    <a title="Q." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4303953-q"><img alt="Q." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472430083p2/4303953.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/216252129?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Q." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Q." href="/user/show/4303953-q">Q.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4303953-q?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer216252129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13130403716920555814">I can see how this comic would have massive cult appeal to the 'disenfranchised youth' of the 90's. However, this book is the bastard child of Strangers in Paradise and Johnny the Homicidal Maniac with a dash of Clerks. It has all the negativity of both books (Plus Daria and Roseanne) but none of the wit, charm or cleverness.<br/><br/>Don't get me wrong, I love negativity. Negativity is awesome if delivered with some class. This book has no class.<br/><br/>Like mommy Strangers in Paradise it features two young woma</span>
  <span id="freeText13130403716920555814" style="display:none">I can see how this comic would have massive cult appeal to the 'disenfranchised youth' of the 90's. However, this book is the bastard child of Strangers in Paradise and Johnny the Homicidal Maniac with a dash of Clerks. It has all the negativity of both books (Plus Daria and Roseanne) but none of the wit, charm or cleverness.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, I love negativity. Negativity is awesome if delivered with some class. This book has no class.<br /><br />Like mommy Strangers in Paradise it features two young woman who are just trying to find their way in the world but like Daddy JtHM, it hates everyone and swears up a storm. <br /><br />Enid and Rebecca are not fun people, they are not interesting people. They are everything they hate and there is nothing endearing about them.<br /><br />The passage of time in the book is...hard to follow, with scenes suddenly ending for new ones. Are these flashbacks? And then suddenly Enid goes off to college then...comes back to visit and Rebecca stays in stupid-head nowhere with the guy? What am I supposed to take away from this? The more things change? <br /><br />The writing wasn't witty or new, it was all the cliche stuff we expect 'nihilistic', misanthropic teenagers say.<br /><br />I will at least give credit where it's due in the sake that they did feel like real people.<br /><br />Real people I'd never hang out with.<br /><br />If you liked this book, I'd recommend Strangers in Paradise for some quality "Who am I and what's my purpose?" story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13130403716920555814" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Estelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17934127-estelle"><img alt="Estelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591320955p2/17934127.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1525731488?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Estelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Estelle" href="/user/show/17934127-estelle">Estelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17934127-estelle?shelf=graphic-novels-manga-bd">graphic-novels-manga-bd</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17934127-estelle?shelf=funny">funny</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1525731488" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1372286966600893549">As a big fan of the movie adaptation I've always been curious but slightly hesitant to read the comic book. Especially after hearing some people weren't too fond of it. <br/><br/>Well, I kinda loved it! It's was a bit weird (the non-linear narrative, the use of only two colors, the bleak ending), but also hilarious, cynical and angsty but without taking itself too seriously (at least imo). <br/>Can't say I personally relate to either Enid or Rebecca, but I felt like I know those girls, I've seen bits and piece</span>
  <span id="freeText1372286966600893549" style="display:none">As a big fan of the movie adaptation I've always been curious but slightly hesitant to read the comic book. Especially after hearing some people weren't too fond of it. <br /><br />Well, I kinda loved it! It's was a bit weird (the non-linear narrative, the use of only two colors, the bleak ending), but also hilarious, cynical and angsty but without taking itself too seriously (at least imo). <br />Can't say I personally relate to either Enid or Rebecca, but I felt like I know those girls, I've seen bits and pieces of them in other people. You might call them mean and unlikeable, but I feel a bit of tenderness for them. <br /><br />I liked it, but I can see why some people wouldn't. I'd say the movie is a lot more accessible and "cool". </span>
  <a data-text-id="1372286966600893549" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1576492956" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1576492956" />
    <a title="Donna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6217162-donna"><img alt="Donna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430955688p2/6217162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1576492956?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna" href="/user/show/6217162-donna">Donna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6217162-donna?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6217162-donna?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1576492956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17201999699501481653">I haven't read very many comics or graphic novels, but I thought I'd explore them more this year starting with this book which kept popping up on "best of" lists in its category.<br/><br/>My first surprise when I opened the book was seeing that every skillfully drawn picture was in black and white and green--a ghostly green--so I guess this made sense considering the book's title and how it and the colors echoed the feeling of limbo and separateness that the main characters had from a more substantial and</span>
  <span id="freeText17201999699501481653" style="display:none">I haven't read very many comics or graphic novels, but I thought I'd explore them more this year starting with this book which kept popping up on "best of" lists in its category.<br /><br />My first surprise when I opened the book was seeing that every skillfully drawn picture was in black and white and green--a ghostly green--so I guess this made sense considering the book's title and how it and the colors echoed the feeling of limbo and separateness that the main characters had from a more substantial and cheerful world full of color. <br /><br />This book focuses on two teenaged girls who have been best friends for years and have recently graduated from high school. They are Enid Coleslaw and Becky Doppelmeyer, <br />two outsiders and self proclaimed hipsters. Enid is foul-mouthed, mean spirited, pessimistic, and constantly angry at everyone, including herself. She's also constantly changing her look on any given day or during any given hour. Becky is somewhat shallow and not much for having deeper thoughts, though she's intelligent, so maybe she simply chooses to not examine things too closely. She pales in comparison to her friend Enid whom she's a follower of in whatever adventures and misadventures Enid becomes involved in. <br /><br />Early in the story, we learn that Enid's father wants his daughter to go away to college and pushes her into taking an entrance exam at a school he's chosen for her. It's not that he's uncaring or overbearing so much as worried and trying to give his daughter some direction, however misdirected this is when not considering her own needs. As Enid waits for the exam results, she and Becky wander through their days and ponder the possibility of their impending separation and the effects it will have on their friendship. <br /><br />This is one of those books that someone can interpret in any number of ways, influencing how it affects them and how they'd judge it. Some people will focus on the story's aimlessness, as well as the negativity dominating the book, most of it coming from Enid as she leads Becky into some cruel practical jokes against unsuspecting friends and strangers alike. And then, there is her constant stream of swear words and crudity, sarcasm and cutting remarks about nearly everyone who crosses her path. Some of it did get to me in this concentrated form, but for some people, this behavior is their reality. And after a while, it became white noise masking something else, as I believe the author intended from such repetition. So what I chose to focus on was what lay below the surface--the causes of this disaffected behavior, which the author slowly reveals, the ending a soft punch to the gut, putting a period on this story or maybe it was more of a question mark. <br /><br />I won't say I enjoyed this book so much as I was absorbed by it and equally fascinated by and sad for the characters, not to mention angry at them, at times. For me to feel so many different things in reaction to a book, I must label it a success. How you feel about it may differ. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17201999699501481653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XELbZcTPZUUF8n5hlMaBe/HWWfHMW/6U2AqOiIgaqGz0ciANrYhGS2pYQov8oTMqUxr8Osmi3a1S9o8XtgO9mg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('f9sesilyP9tx8eidY428P/8zTV5cQNeF1i7dIIwHnEHX6+XaQDUc1R5b1HcL6g5uXf/olVm59Lxc0ty/sh6Jtw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer15890233480253513762">Daniel Gillespie Clowes is an Academy Award-nominated American author, screenwriter and cartoonist of alternative comic books. Most of Clowes' work appears first in his anthology <i>Eightball</i> (1989-2004), a collection of self-contained narratives and serialized graphic novels. Several of these narratives have been collected published separately as graphic novels, most notably <i>Ghost World</i>. With filmma</span>
  <span id="freeText15890233480253513762" style="display:none">Daniel Gillespie Clowes is an Academy Award-nominated American author, screenwriter and cartoonist of alternative comic books. Most of Clowes' work appears first in his anthology <i>Eightball</i> (1989-2004), a collection of self-contained narratives and serialized graphic novels. Several of these narratives have been collected published separately as graphic novels, most notably <i>Ghost World</i>. With filmmaker Terry Zwigoff, Clowes adapted <i>Ghost World</i> into the 2000 film of the same name, and also adapted another <i>Eightball</i> story into the 2006 film <i>Art School Confidential</i>. Before <i>Eightball</i>, Clowes worked on comic book series Lloyd Llewellyn, which in the later issues stronger foreshadowed some of the social criticism of his work with <i>Eightball</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15890233480253513762" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
